  The root cause is prose stuffed into table cells. A markdown table is for
  short, columnar, scannable values вҖ” the moment a cell holds a paragraph, the
  table deforms (for you) and becomes one unsplittable source line (for me вҖ” I
  can't target a sub-part of a 7k-char cell to edit it precisely; I have to
  rewrite the whole thing each unit). Bullets and prose wrap fine, so tasks.md
  is tolerable; the two tables are the real problem.

  My recommendation, in priority order:

  1. IMPLEMENTATION.md В§3 вҖ” the big win. That 7k cell is the per-unit narrative,
  and it's duplicated almost verbatim in tasks.md (the U-bullets) вҖ” which is
  why I've been updating the same wall of text in two places every unit. Fix:
  make В§3 a genuine at-a-glance dashboard (terse one-line status per phase) and
  point to tasks.md / the decisions ledger for per-unit detail. Removes the
  deformation and the duplication.

  | Phase | Status |
  |---|---|
  | 1. Requirements | вң… APPROVED (2026-05-29) |
  | 2. Design       | вң… APPROVED & merged to main (2026-05-29) |
  | 3. Tasks        | рҹҹҰ IN PROGRESS вҖ” P1вҖ“P4 вң…; P5 units U1вҖ“U11 вң…, U12вҖ“U16
  left; P6 left |

  Per-unit detail: tasks.md В§P5. Decisions & open loops: decisions.md.

  2. decisions.md вҖ” convert the per-phase log from a table to headed entries.
  Each decision becomes a short **ID** вҖ” decision line + _Why:_ prose (a
  definition-list shape) instead of a paragraph-in-a-cell. Reads better, diffs
  cleanly, no width limit.

  3. tasks.md вҖ” optional. Bullets don't deform; if anything, break each unit's
  run-on into 2вҖ“3 sub-bullets (what / lab+refs / traceability). Lowest value.

  A note on "a better format than markdown": for the structured facts (which
  unit is done, which refs exist) the machine-readable meta/* artifacts are
  already the right home вҖ” the spec docs should stay prose-for-humans, just not
  prose-in-tables.

  This is your spec's convention, so let me confirm scope before editing:

в—Ҹ Done and pushed. Here's the answer to your question and what I changed.

  The diagnosis

  The readability problem wasn't markdown itself вҖ” it was prose stuffed into 
  table cells. A markdown table is for short, columnar, scannable values; the
  moment a cell holds a paragraph it deforms visually (and becomes one
  unsplittable source line that's painful to diff/edit). The fix is to keep 
  tables for short data and move accumulating narrative to prose/bullets.

  What I did (all three files)
